<div id="review_426011566" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/426011566" />
    <a title="Sarah (saz101)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3825460-sarah-saz101"><img alt="Sarah (saz101)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1300234087p2/3825460.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/426011566?book_show_action=true">Oct 01, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Sarah (saz101)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Sarah (saz101)" href="/user/show/3825460-sarah-saz101">Sarah (saz101)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780732294700" href="/book/show/15852507-what-s-left-of-me">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3825460-sarah-saz101?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3825460-sarah-saz101?shelf=dystopia">dystopia</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer426011566" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3903282461534204172"><strong>
  <em>3.5 Stars</em>
</strong><br/><br/>From the post-apocalyptic wastelands of Obernewtyn, to the stark contrasts of poverty and lavish opulence in Pan Am, Dystopian – YA’s enduring wunderkind – comes in many shapes and sizes, and never has it seemed it so normal and suburban, yet so alien, cruel and <em>wrong</em> as in the alternate reality of Kat Zhang's <em>What’s Left of Me</em>.<br/><br/><b>The Story</b><br/>It's an accepted certainty that every person is born with two souls, two girls or two boys, opening their shared eyes for the first time, as separat</span>
  <span id="freeText3903282461534204172" style="display:none"><strong>
  <em>3.5 Stars</em>
</strong><br /><br />From the post-apocalyptic wastelands of Obernewtyn, to the stark contrasts of poverty and lavish opulence in Pan Am, Dystopian – YA’s enduring wunderkind – comes in many shapes and sizes, and never has it seemed it so normal and suburban, yet so alien, cruel and <em>wrong</em> as in the alternate reality of Kat Zhang's <em>What’s Left of Me</em>.<br /><br /><b>The Story</b><br />It's an accepted certainty that every person is born with two souls, two girls or two boys, opening their shared eyes for the first time, as separate and unique as they are one and whole.<br /><br />It's just as certain that one of those souls will evanesce. Dominant and recessive, one soul born to lead, and to live, the other destined to disappear. Two children within the body of one, with their family, friends, and their world, expecting one to die. <em>Hoping</em> one will fade.<br /><br />Addie and Eva, Eva and Addie are two such souls. Addie, strong, in control, destined to live, and Eva, destined to... not. But Eva didn't fade when it was her time. Eva clung to life, and now the two girls go about their life, Addie leading, and Eva an ever-present witness, both hiding. Because having two souls, being a 'hybrid', is illegal. Eva and Addie hide in plain sight, from everyone. Even their family. Until someone notices the girl hiding inside, and offers her the unthinkable: a chance to walk again. To breathe. To speak. Trapped inside her sister's body for years, how could they say no?<br /> The 101 <br />While, in many ways, Kat Zhang’s debut is an introspective, reflective story, it also carries in its pages a suffocating unfairness, an immense corruption and cruelty that seeps deep enough to rattle bones. I’ve always felt this ‘type’ of novel can go two ways: leaving the protagonist – and reader – feeling empowered, rallied, ready to fight; or adrift in a world of corruption so vast they feel hopeless. What’s Left Of Me left <em>me</em> feeling frightened and small, unconvinced that, hybrid or not, a protagonist so ‘ordinary’ and powerless, so much a normal schoolgirl, could ever overcome a system and government so corrupt, and, honestly, I’m not entirely sure how that makes me feel, or how I feel about the book on a whole.<br /><br />While it may sound oxymoronic, the lack of grounding in our world, the sense of <em>‘this could really happen</em>, gives What’s Left Of Me a fantastical feel, but also robs it of frightening impact often granted by the same, yet it feels peculiar to comment on as, in all ways but the obvious – of two souls sharing a single body – there is a profound sense of normalcy to What’s Left Of Me, and an almost Stepford-like suburbia. But this suburbia doesn’t last for long, and despite sixteen years of practice for Addie/Eva, neither does the ‘normal’ façade.’<br /><br />The relationship between Addie and Eva is the tale’s strongest facet, their pull and push, and the conflict between two very different people with very different desires forced to share one body, one life, is beautiful and painful to witness. This aspect alone is enough to make What’s Left of Me compelling, but a book is never <em>one</em> thing: Animal Farm is not a story solely about talking Animals, and The Hunger Games is not only a story about a girl who’s a decent shot with a bow falling for a baker. Great books are the product of many pieces falling into place cohesively. What’s Left Of Me was like a jigsaw with matching shapes, but not colours.<br /><br />When we talk of series – and What’s Left Of Me is planned as a trilogy, I believe – it’s not uncommon to hear the term ‘Middle Book Syndrome’ referring to a slump mid-series, or a book two which serves as little more than filler. What’s Left Of Me, being book one, does not have this problem, but ‘Middle <em>Of The</em> Book Syndrome’ may be a more appropriate term. A shocking change in scenery mid-book lends the book a very different – and far darker – tone than that with which it starts, but it also trips pacing. It’s worth noting What’s Left Of Me is very much a character-driven story, but its contemplative tone has moments teetering dangerously close to dull in what should be the novel’s most tense moments.<br /><br />While What’s Left Of Me is not without its flaws, it remains a lovely story. Quiet, meditative, heavy with stifling oppression, it offers moments of extraordinary insight. Reflecting on what we leave behind as we turn from youth to adulthood – in the case of this world something profound and tangible – What’s Left of Me serves as powerful allegory for the sacrifice of self, of youth, of the self-imposed requirement to conform we each battle.<br /><br /><b>The Verdict:</b><br />Filled with achingly beautiful moments of contemplation, and a dystopian side so oppressive, suffocating and cruel in its subtleties and familiarities it’s crushing, What’s Left Of Me is a wonderfully unique story. The concept is extraordinary, and the interplay, the push and pull, the balance between Addie and Eva is compelling and beautiful and heartbreaking. At its worst, it dances close by the boundary of boring, but at its best? It’s <em>breathtaking</em>. I liked What’s Left Of Me. A compelling start to a very promising series.</span>
  <a data-text-id="3903282461534204172" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_279413897" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/279413897" />
    <a title="Jen (The Starry-Eyed Revue)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4659650-jen-the-starry-eyed-revue"><img alt="Jen (The Starry-Eyed Revue)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1390185382p2/4659650.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/279413897?book_show_action=true">Feb 17, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jen (The Starry-Eyed Revue)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jen (The Starry-Eyed Revue)" href="/user/show/4659650-jen-the-starry-eyed-revue">Jen (The Starry-Eyed Revue)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4659650-jen-the-starry-eyed-revue?shelf=aliens-sci-fi">aliens-sci-fi</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4659650-jen-the-starry-eyed-revue?shelf=dystopian-post-apocalyptic">dystopian-post-apocalyptic</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4659650-jen-the-starry-eyed-revue?shelf=edelweiss">edelweiss</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4659650-jen-the-starry-eyed-revue?shelf=souls-afterlife">souls-afterlife</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4659650-jen-the-starry-eyed-revue?shelf=2012">2012</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer279413897" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4101031757837465011">**4 1/2 stars**<br/><br/>So, it’s been awhile since I’ve read <i>The Golden Compass</i> and even longer still since I’ve seen <i>Girl, Interruped</i>, but I don’t think a cross between those is how I would pitch this novel. No, I think the comparisons to Meyer’s <i>The Host</i> are more apt, and though I appreciated that book quite a bit more than I expected to after reading <i>Twilight</i>, I still think <i>What’s Left of Me</i> handles the symbiotic relationship between two souls in a more fascinating manner. I’m not thumbing my nose at </span>
  <span id="freeText4101031757837465011" style="display:none">**4 1/2 stars**<br /><br />So, it’s been awhile since I’ve read <i>The Golden Compass</i> and even longer still since I’ve seen <i>Girl, Interruped</i>, but I don’t think a cross between those is how I would pitch this novel. No, I think the comparisons to Meyer’s <i>The Host</i> are more apt, and though I appreciated that book quite a bit more than I expected to after reading <i>Twilight</i>, I still think <i>What’s Left of Me</i> handles the symbiotic relationship between two souls in a more fascinating manner. I’m not thumbing my nose at <i>The Host</i> by any means, though…I’m still as excited for the movie as the rest of you guys. :)<br /><br />I think I expected <i>What’s Left of Me</i> to be slow and methodical: a science fiction piece exploring the inner dialogue between two souls and the complexities that arise as they fight for control of one body. And there was plenty of that. But what I hadn’t expected was the external prodding to coexist that the two souls were faced with and where it came from. And how they reacted to such prompting. To say that there were lots of twists and unpredictable situations would be an understatement.<br /><br />So…plenty of action, but also beaucoups of emotion, as well. It was so difficult to read from Eva’s point-of-view. She was the lesser soul, the one who was supposed to fade as Addie’s soul grew more dominant. To be trapped like that, inside your own body, and know that no one misses you…it’s unimaginable. And yet that’s the fate that Eva has suffered for the last three years because no one but Addie even knows she’s still there, desperate to move of her own volition.<br /><br />This book could cause one to have an existential crisis. Dissociative identity disorder is a very real and very serious mental ailment. But what if it were really the manifestation of two souls battling for domination over one mind? Essentially, that’s what’s happening in Hybrids, where two souls remain past the age where one should have faded into nothingness. When other Hybrids were around Addie/Eva, you would have thought it would be difficult to discern which soul was present, but I never found it confusing or distracting, as Eva would always remark upon the change. And the way she described it was nothing like I expected, which was more like a person morphing into a Smith from <i>The Matrix</i>. No, the shift in a Hybrid was very subtle, just a straightening of features, a crook of the mouth, or a glint in the eyes that marked the change.<br /><br />This is very much a science fiction novel, full of government conspiracies, sterile labs, and barely legal medical testing. If you read for romance, you might be slightly disappointed with this novel, because though the implications are there, the romance is hardly expanded upon and it takes a backseat to everything else in the book. But in my opinion, the book is better for it. How would you feel if the other entity living inside your head wanted to kiss someone you didn’t even really like? Yeah…I thought so.<br /><br /><i>Thanks to HarperCollins for providing a galley for review.</i><br /><br />This review and others can be found at <a href="http://starryeyedrevue.blogspot.com/2012/09/review-whats-left-of-me-by-kat-zhang.html" rel="nofollow noopener">The Starry-Eyed Revue</a>.</span>
  <a data-text-id="4101031757837465011" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_411448421" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/411448421" />
    <a title="Nemo (The Moonlight Library)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/11289146-nemo-the-moonlight-library"><img alt="Nemo (The Moonlight Library)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1560136145p2/11289146.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/411448421?book_show_action=true">Sep 10, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Nemo (The Moonlight Library)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Nemo (The Moonlight Library)" href="/user/show/11289146-nemo-the-moonlight-library">Nemo (The Moonlight Library)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780732294700" href="/book/show/15852507-what-s-left-of-me">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11289146-nemo-the-moonlight-library?shelf=the-tempest-of-my-eyes">the-tempest-of-my-eyes</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11289146-nemo-the-moonlight-library?shelf=publisher-5-harpercollins">publisher-5-harpercollins</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11289146-nemo-the-moonlight-library?shelf=beautiful-covers">beautiful-covers</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11289146-nemo-the-moonlight-library?shelf=arc">arc</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11289146-nemo-the-moonlight-library?shelf=books-i-own">books-i-own</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11289146-nemo-the-moonlight-library?shelf=2012-read">2012-read</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11289146-nemo-the-moonlight-library?shelf=2012-favourites">2012-favourites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11289146-nemo-the-moonlight-library?shelf=source-netgalley">source-netgalley</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer411448421" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15720885693932843269"><b>See <a href='http://moonlightlibrary.wordpress.com/2012/10/01/arc-book-review-whats-left-of-me-by-kat-zhang/' rel='nofollow noopener'>this review</a> and more on <a href='http://moonlightlibrary.wordpress.com/' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Moonlight Library</a>!</b><br/><br/>Kat Zhang’s lushly imagined What’s Left of Me spins the tale of what happens when a recessive soul sharing one body with a dominant soul refuses to fade away, as they’ve been led to believe is inevitable. Anyone left with two souls in theor single body is a ‘hybrid – dangerous, illegal, and swiftly dealt with by the government. Eva is our recessive soul, and the book is told from her point of view. She shares a body with Addie, and they are fifte</span>
  <span id="freeText15720885693932843269" style="display:none"><b>See <a href="http://moonlightlibrary.wordpress.com/2012/10/01/arc-book-review-whats-left-of-me-by-kat-zhang/" rel="nofollow noopener">this review</a> and more on <a href="http://moonlightlibrary.wordpress.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">The Moonlight Library</a>!</b><br /><br />Kat Zhang’s lushly imagined What’s Left of Me spins the tale of what happens when a recessive soul sharing one body with a dominant soul refuses to fade away, as they’ve been led to believe is inevitable. Anyone left with two souls in theor single body is a ‘hybrid – dangerous, illegal, and swiftly dealt with by the government. Eva is our recessive soul, and the book is told from her point of view. She shares a body with Addie, and they are fifteen years old.<br /><br />Although I really loved this book, I felt that the writing was aimed a bit younger than Eva and Addie’s age. Telling the book from Eva’s point of view was wonderful – Eva reported everything Addie did, but couldn’t tell what her sister-soul was thinking unless they shared thoughts. I loved the whole concept – it reminded me of some of my favourite Animorphs novels, where (usually) Cassie shared a mind with either another Yeerk or another soul, and often spoke to them mind-to-mind. This way of writing made me instantly smitten, and I adored Zhang’s poetic storytelling skill as she wove Eva re-learning how to use her body and gain the control she naturally lacks.<br /><br />Eva and Addie were wonderful to read about. I liked seeing the world from Eva’s point of view, and seeing how much Addie, the dominant soul, needed her recessive sister. Although it’s never exactly explained why hybrids are so dangerous (propaganda plays a huge part in this novel) I could easily see how scatter-brained, artistic Addie needed her more logical, rational sister-soul to keep them both functioning at the highest level. You’d normally expect the flowery, artistic-type, often portrayed as nerds or wallflowers in other media – to be the recessive soul and the wilful, scrappy soul to be the dominant one, so it was really interesting seeing how the relationship between the two played out. It was also fascinating watching the other hybrids interacting, switching between souls, and never getting confused by the change of names of the same character. It was unbelievable well-written and wonderfully pulled off.<br /><br />The only disappointment in this book is, I think, in the lack of different locations. It basically takes place at Eva and Addie’s school, their house, their friend Hally’s house, or the facility known as Nornand. I did get a little bit bored in the Nornand section only because the location never changed and despite Eva and Addie’s planning, everything seemed to go wrong and I clutched at my hair screaming internally at Zhang, “WHY ARE YOU SO MEAN TO YOUR BABIES?!”<br /><br />But apart from that, and the terrible anxiety I got reading this novel and willing everything to work out for Eva and Addie, I really loved this and I look forward to reading Book 2. It’s original, heartbreaking, and really makes you think about propaganda, the government, what it’s like to be a child, the power of the medical world, international relations and all sorts of things. It was wonderful.<br /><br />4.5 stars.<br /><br /><i>An advance reader copy was kindly provided by the publisher.</i></span>
  <a data-text-id="15720885693932843269" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

		<td>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('mPcP5khbYsvOJ8TO6BdYbvudovdNfEybFvGbHAGcVqkS1zDGm199UjlZyR+EhniKQTjq8/UO2tXcYHpsVVauew==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('8heP51zPjq676mt4ntzvj5u15GoWFT2bSRQZ49pC7u54N7DHj8uRN0yUZqnyTc9rIRCsbq5nq9WDhfiTjogWPA==')})
  }

Made by the Weavers as a copy of someone else, she is expected to replace a girl named Amarra, her “other”, if she ever died. Eva studies what Amarra does, what she eats, what it’s like to kiss her boyfriend, Ray. So when Amarra is killed in a car crash, Eva should be ready.\n\nBut fifteen years of studying never prepared her for this.\n\nNow she must abandon everything she’s ever known—the guardians who raised her, the boy she’s forbidden to love—to move to India and convince the world that Amarra is still alive.\n\nWhat Eva finds is a grief-stricken family; parents unsure how to handle this echo they thought they wanted; and Ray, who knew every detail, every contour of Amarra. And when Eva is unexpectedly dealt a fatal blow that will change her existence forever, she is forced to choose: Stay and live out her years as a copy or leave and risk it all for the freedom to be an original. <span id="freeTextContainer4234334846639677744">*Please do not message me through Goodreads! Instead, email me at katzhang3 AT gmail DOT com. I don't get on Goodreads often to check messages! Thank you :) *<br/><br/><br/>Kat Zhang spent most of her childhood tramping through a world weaved from her favorite stories and games. When she and her best friend weren't riding magic horses or talking to trees, they were writing adaptations of plays for their stuffed </span>
  <span id="freeText4234334846639677744" style="display:none">*Please do not message me through Goodreads! Instead, email me at katzhang3 AT gmail DOT com. I don't get on Goodreads often to check messages! Thank you :) *<br /><br /><br />Kat Zhang spent most of her childhood tramping through a world weaved from her favorite stories and games. When she and her best friend weren't riding magic horses or talking to trees, they were writing adaptations of plays for their stuffed animals (what would The Wizard of Oz have been like if the Cowardly Lion were replaced by a Loquacious Lamb?). This may or may not explain many of Kat's quirks today.<br /><br />By the age of twelve, Kat had started her first novel and begun plans for her life as a Real Live Author (she was rather more confident at twelve than she is even now). Said plans didn't come into fruition until seven years later, when her agent sold her Young Adult trilogy, The Hybrid Chronicles, to HarperCollins. The series, about a parallel universe where everyone is born with two souls, concluded in 2014.<br /><br />Her two upcoming Middle Grade novels will be released in 2017 and 2018 with Simon &amp; Schuster. The first, The Emperor's Riddle, is about hidden treasure, lost aunts, and China. The second, The Memory of Forgotten Things, is about parallel universes (again), solar eclipses, and misfit children.<br /><br />Kat is represented by Emmanuelle Morgen of Stonesong. She also contributes to Pub(lishing) Crawl, a site for aspiring writers to talk about books, storytelling craft, and the publishing process.</span>
